dealings between Coinbase, the biggest crypto exchange in America, and BlackRock, the largest asset manager in the world, may not be entirely on the up and up. Though a flood of capital into new spot Bitcoin ETFs pushed the price of BTC to a new all-time high in March, just two months after ETFs were approved in the U.S., the price should be much higher today with all those billions flowing into the market, befuddled Bitcoin buyers say. Coinbase‚Äîthe U.S.-based cryptocurrency exchange that serves as custodian for most Bitcoin ETFs, including BlackRock‚Äîmust not actually be buying the Bitcoin requested by these funds, and instead merely issuing ‚ÄúIOUs,‚Äù or ‚Äúpaper‚Äù Bitcoin, these critics say. The unsubstantiated rumors echoed throughout social media over the last few months, and eventually became loud enough that Coinbase CEO Brian Armstrong addressed the concerns on X, formerly known as Twitter. ‚ÄúNot sure what this is all about [to be honest],‚Äù he said last week. ‚ÄúAll ETF mints and burns we process are ultimately settled on-chain.‚Äù Just two days later, however, BlackRock filed an amendment to its ETF registration with the SEC which now requires Coinbase to release Bitcoin much quicker to the asset manager, within 12 hours of notice, when BlackRock customers buy shares of its Bitcoin ETF product. Critics latched onto the update as evidence that their worries were not unfounded. Baldilocks here. Not sure what this is all about TBH. All ETF mints and burns we process are ultimately settled onchain. Institutional clients have trade financing and OTC options before trades are settled onchain. This is the norm for all our institutional clients. All funds‚Ä¶ ‚Äî Brian Armstrong (@brian_armstrong) September 14, 2024 But it‚Äôs all hogwash, says Bloomberg ETF analyst Eric Balchunas. ‚ÄúI‚Äôve been tracking [the ETF] industry for 20 years, and there‚Äôs never been a case of this stuff not being with the custodian,‚Äù he told Decrypt. ‚ÄúFirst of all, it‚Äôd be illegal.‚Äù The idea that an ETF issuer or its custodian may not actually hold the underlying asset isn‚Äôt new. As Balchunas pointed out on X, it‚Äôs a worry that some gold investors have shared about gold ETFs for years. pic.twitter.com/u6lupDrOgs ‚Äî Eric Balchunas (@EricBalchunas) September 16, 2024 An ETF is a way for investors to gain exposure to an asset, like gold or Bitcoin, without actually holding the asset themselves. With Bitcoin ETFs, for example, investors buy shares in BlackRock‚Äôs fund, and BlackRock then buys a corresponding amount of Bitcoin and stores it on Coinbase. There are trade-offs, though, and the added convenience requires an element of trust‚Äîand risk. Skeptical Bitcoiners would rather see on-chain receipts than receive assurances. The idea that Coinbase may be issuing paper Bitcoin to BlackRock dates back to at least May, when the pseudonymous trader ‚ÄúTyler Durden,‚Äù who holds a sizable audience on X, began the charge. ‚ÄúBlackrock can take as much Bitcoin as they want from Coinbase and the transaction is recorded off chain,‚Äù he tweeted. The post currently has 1.6 million views. Earlier this month, music producer and crypto trader MartyParty fanned the flames, claiming that the price of Bitcoin is not moving upwards despite BlackRock ‚Äúbuying all the Bitcoin.‚Äù ‚ÄúScam of the century,‚Äù he wrote. Balchunas dismissed the claims as a ‚Äúconspiracy theory.‚Äù ‚ÄúThis isn‚Äôt like FTX, where you just throw up an exchange out of nowhere, and some buffoon is running it from a Bahama penthouse,‚Äù he told Decrypt. ‚Äú[BlackRock] is a serious company which has dozens of lawyers. They‚Äôre not gonna jeopardize their hard won reputation, let alone get sued by all the investors,‚Äù he said. Balchunas yesterday confirmed on X that he had spoken with BlackRock to find out more. He said that the asset manager runs ‚Äúits own blockchain node‚Äù and pulls the BTC balances from their wallet addresses to put on Coinbase Prime every night. He said the firm can show balances to clients if requested, but would never make them public as they could get hit with spam such as dusting (when crypto users send small quantities of Bitcoin to wallet addresses to track, taint, or de-anonymize them.) BlackRock declined to respond to Decrypt‚Äôs questions, instead pointing to an interview Robbie Mitchnick, the firm‚Äôs head of digital assets, gave Bloomberg on Tuesday. When asked about last week‚Äôs controversial filing regarding Coinbase, he said it was a ‚Äúnormal course update‚Äù and that ‚Äúnothing of significance has changed.‚Äù A Coinbase spokesperson confirmed to Decrypt that the unsubstantiated rumors being pushed on X were just that and nothing more, adding that regulatory updates were normal. No conspiracies. Nothing of significance has changed. This is a normal course update. https://t.co/kAk0NQI1yV ‚Äî Jaclyn Sales üõ°Ô∏è (@MsJaclynSales) September 25, 2024 BlackRock‚Äôs IBIT is the biggest and most successful of the ETFs now trading in the U.S. The fund currently holds 357,732 BTC, according to its website, worth around $22.6 billion. Bitcoin‚Äôs price is now up over 140% over the past year, CoinGecko data shows, with the price surging following the approval of the ETFs. ‚ÄúI say you take that as a win,‚Äù said Balchunas, referring to Bitcoin‚Äôs price. ‚ÄúIt could be way worse.‚Äù ‚ÄúI mean, what price would make you happy?‚Äù Your gateway into the world of Web3 The latest news, articles, and resources, sent to your inbox weekly. ¬© A next-generation media company. 2024 Decrypt Media, Inc.

Title: [EU] Blackrock Depths Raid Testing Schedule
URL: https://www.bluetracker.gg/wow/topic/eu-en/539838-blackrock-depths-raid-testing-schedule/
Time Published: 2024-09-25T21:32:33Z
Full Content:
Hi everyone, The time has come to test the upcoming raid encounters in The War Within: 20th Anniversary Update, and the team is very excited to hear your feedback. We‚Äôd like to remind everyone that the raid testing schedule is fluid and subject to the realities of a test environment. We may have to change the time of a testing session, change the boss(es) being tested, or cancel a test entirely due to bugs, server hardware issues, etc. Keep an eye on this forum for the boss feedback threads and latest information. Thank you in advance for testing, critical feedback is invaluable to us and helps us understand where to make iterative improvements during development. Start: 11:00 PDT (14:00 EDT, 20:00 CEST) End: 11:00 PDT (14:00 EDT, 20:00 CEST) the following day Start: 11:00 PDT (14:00 EDT, 20:00 CEST) End: 11:00 PDT (14:00 EDT, 20:00 CEST) the following day Start: 11:00 PDT (14:00 EDT, 20:00 CEST) End: 11:00 PDT (14:00 EDT, 20:00 CEST) the following day Start: 11:00 PDT (14:00 EDT, 20:00 CEST) End: 11:00 PDT (14:00 EDT, 20:00 CEST) the following day Q: How do I get into the raid zone? A: In Dornogal, Orgrimmar, or Stormwind, you may speak to Nexus-Lord Donjon Rade V in order to teleport into the raid zone while it is open for testing. Q: What character should I use to test the raid? A: Whichever you prefer. We will be scaling players‚Äô effective level to 80 for raid testing, and their item level to an appropriate threshold for the encounter(s) being tested. Q: How long does testing last? A: The primary purpose of testing is to give us the information we need to balance the encounters, evaluate how mechanics are playing out in practice, and identify bugs. 20th Anniversary raid testing will be available for 24 hours after they‚Äôve been enabled. Q: How do I report feedback or bugs? A: We‚Äôll be posting encounter feedback threads each week prior to the start of the raid tests. Additionally, you can also submit your feedback through the in-game Issue Reporter tool. We appreciate you taking the time to test our content and look forward to reading your feedback.

Title: XRP Price Explosion Finally In The Cards as Grayscale XRP Trust Turns Game-Changer For XRP-Based ETF
URL: https://zycrypto.com/xrp-price-explosion-finally-in-the-cards-as-grayscale-xrp-trust-turns-game-changer-for-xrp-based-etf/
Time Published: 2024-09-25T21:19:12Z
Full Content:
Ripple‚Äôs XRP is on a massive uptrend, gaining 7.7% in the seven days. The gains come after the world‚Äôs largest digital asset manager, Grayscale, announced plans to launch the first XRP Trust in the US. According to Grayscale, the launch of the XRP Trust is the first step towards the digital asset manager launching an exchange-traded fund (ETF) for XRP. ‚ÄúWe believe Grayscale XRP Trust provides investors with exposure to a blockchain solution that is potentially positioned to play a crucial role in optimizing legacy financial systems by streamlining cross-border payments,‚Äù said the head of product and research at Grayscale, Rayhaneh Sharif-Askary. The product will operate as a ‚Äúclosed-end‚Äù fund that will expose investors to XRP. The firm noted that the trust will be rolled out gradually in four phases, and an ETF is planned for later. Grayscale is the main force behind the approval of spot crypto ETFs in the US. Last year, the asset manager sued the US Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) to convert its Grayscale Bitcoin Trust to a spot ETF tracking BTC‚Äôs spot price. After Grayscale won the court case, Wall Street giants BlackRock and Fidelity launched their crypto ETFs. Grayscale‚Äôs Bitcoin and Ethereum ETFs are also among the largest in the US. The launch of this product also comes amid uncertainty over whether the SEC might appeal a judge‚Äôs ruling that XRP secondary sales are not securities. As ZyCrypto reported, the Ripple legal team sought court approval to delay payment for the $125M settlement. The Grayscale XRP Trust will join the growing list of crypto funds managed by Grayscale. The crypto asset manager also offers trusts for other altcoins, including Avalanche and Solana. XRP price jumped by more than 8% after the development to trade at $0.58. Trading volumes also shot up by as high as 80% per CoinMarketCap. The news saw XRP reach the highest level since late August, outperforming the rest of the top ten largest cryptos by market capitalization. According to an analyst on X, XRP has formed a bullish ascending triangle, with a breakout possibly taking the prices to levels above $0.70. This could pave the way for a rally to $1, especially if the trust attracts institutional investors.

Title: Bitcoin ETFs are less than 200,000 BTC away from surpassing Satoshi Nakamoto‚Äôs holdings
URL: https://cryptoslate.com/bitcoin-etfs-are-less-than-200000-btc-away-from-surpassing-satoshi-nakamotos-holdings/
Time Published: 2024-09-25T19:15:37Z
Full Content:
The Bitcoin creator is estimated to have 1.1 million BTC, 17% more than the Bitcoin ETFs' combined stash of 916,047 BTC stash as of Sept. 24. Cover art/illustration via CryptoSlate. Image includes combined content which may include AI-generated content. Spot Bitcoin (BTC) exchange-traded funds (ETFs) have amassed more than 900,000 BTC since their launch and will soon surpass the 1.1 million BTC held in wallets believed to be owned by Bitcoin‚Äôs pseudonymous creator Satoshi Nakamoto. Bloomberg senior ETF analyst Eric Balchunas recently shared a list of spot Bitcoin ETF holdings, highlighting their cumulative 916,047 BTC stash as of Sept. 24. He noted that the ETFs are close to surpassing the 1 million BTC threshold cumulatively and just 17% shy of surpassing Nakamoto‚Äôs estimated stash. At the current price of $63,622.03, reaching 1 million BTC equates to over $63.6 billion. BlackRock‚Äôs iShares Bitcoin Trust ETF (IBIT) holds the largest amount among the US-traded funds, with 358,080 BTC, while Grayscale‚Äôs ETFs, GBTC and Grayscale Mini Trust (BTC), collectively hold 258,671 BTC. Rounding out the top 3 is Fidelity‚Äôs ETF FBTC, which holds 184,490 BTC. Together, these three Bitcoin ETFs represent nearly 86% of the BTC held by 11 US-traded ETFs. Shaun Edmondson, author of the list shared by Balchunas, noted that Fidelity holds roughly 100,000 BTC as a custodian for MicroStrategy. However, those were not included in the report. Notably, BlackRock added nearly 530 BTC to its wallets over the past 24 hours, according to on-chain data. The last time the asset manager bought Bitcoin was one week ago, through a 273 BTC transfer from Coinbase Prime vaults. Spot Bitcoin exchange-traded funds (ETF) reached $17.8 billion in total flows on Sept. 24, as per Farside Investors‚Äô data. This new mark was reached after four consecutive days of inflows, which totaled roughly $391 million. Fidelity‚Äôs FBTC led the charge by registering $117.7 million in positive flows. BlackRock‚Äôs IBIT followed closely with $110.4 million in inflows, despite not registering activity in two out of the four last trading days. The significant amount is then due to nearly $99 million in cash flowing to IBIT yesterday. ARK 21Shares‚Äô ARKB wrapped up the list of Bitcoin ETFs with over $100 million in inflows, showing $103.1 million in positive net flows in four trading days. Title: Tucker Carlson Bizarrely Claims Alex Jones is ‚ÄòVindicated on Everything‚Äô
URL: https://www.thedailybeast.com/tucker-carlson-bizarrely-claims-alex-jones-is-vindicated-on-everything
Time Published: 2024-09-25T16:19:24Z
Full Content:
SEARCH The right-wing figures appear to be as buddy-buddy as ever, with Alex Jones telling Tucker Carlson on stage Tuesday, ‚ÄúI gotta say, I love you.‚Äù Breaking News Reporter Tucker Carlson‚Äôs embracing of the right-wing fringes reached a new extreme Tuesday after he welcomed the infamous, mass-shooting-denying conspiracist Alex Jones on stage with him as part of his speaking tour. Carlson, addressing a crowd of paying attendees in Pennsylvania, sung Jones‚Äô praises and said he was ‚Äúproud‚Äù to be alongside the 50-year-old Infowars founder who he said has been ‚Äúvindicated on everything.‚Äù Carlson, 55, went as far as calling the far-right provocateur ‚Äúthe most extraordinary person‚Äù he‚Äôd ever met. That‚Äôs a sharp contrast from Carlson‚Äôs comments about Jones in Jan. 2012, when he said Jones, who was then peddling Sept. 11 attacks conspiracies, ‚Äúfreaks me out.‚Äù Carlson‚Äôs glowing statements about Jones on Tuesday is sure to enrage the families of Sandy Hook victims, who lost their elementary-aged loved ones in a horrific mass slaying in 2012 that Jones repeatedly claimed was a hoax carried out by crisis actors. Jones didn‚Äôt just keep his cooky beliefs to himself, unfortunately. He led a smear campaign against the grieving parents of victims, which led to incessant harassment in what was likely the lowest moment of their lives. That hateful conduct is what has Jones on the hook for $1.4 billion as part of a pair of defamation judgements against him in Texas and Connecticut. Those judgements also appear to be killing off InfoWars as we know it. A bankruptcy court said Tuesday it would auction off the assets of Infowars‚Äô parent company, which will see it sell off everything from lighting fixtures to Jones‚Äô dubious vitamin and supplement store. All of that money will then be directed to the families impacted by his lies. With Jones‚Äô personal outlet for spilling his rage now in its final days, he might find a new platform at Carlson‚Äôs side. He already sat down for an interview with Carlson in June and certainly appeared buddy-buddy with him again on Tuesday, telling the former network news host in his intro, ‚ÄúI gotta say, I love you.‚Äù Jones went on to speak with his typical fiery rhetoric, declaring that if Donald Trump is elected again, ‚Äúall of us, together, are going to lift the curse off of this country and we‚Äôre going to send the globalists to prison.‚Äù Jones added that he could ‚Äúfeel the strength in this auditorium‚Äù on Tuesday night. ‚ÄúIt is amazing to meet all these great people,‚Äù Jones said, ‚Äúwhether they‚Äôre Black, white, old, young, to see the electricity in people‚Äôs eyes that are populist and that are Americans and that love God and that love children and love freedom and hate tyranny.‚Äù Carlson interrupted Jones shortly after, saying: ‚ÄúIt just makes me laugh. Oh, you‚Äôre so radical!‚Äù Jones then took back the spotlight, using it to again rail against ‚Äúglobalists.‚Äù ‚ÄúI‚Äôm for the war, peacefully with information, against the globalists,‚Äù he said. ‚ÄúThe real war is here with the globalists and [George] Soros and [Barack] Obama and the New World Order and [investment firm] BlackRock. Title: SEC Postpones Decision To Open Up Options Trading On BlackRock‚Äôs Ethereum ETF Following Bitcoin Nod
URL: https://zycrypto.com/sec-postpones-decision-to-open-up-options-trading-on-blackrocks-ethereum-etf-following-bitcoin-nod/
Time Published: 2024-09-25T15:38:30Z
Full Content:
The United States Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) has delayed deciding on Nasdaq‚Äôs proposed rule change to allow the listing and trading of options on BlackRock‚Äôs Ethereum exchange-traded fund (ETF), the iShares Ethereum Trust (ETHA). This comes despite the SEC recently approving options trading for BlackRock‚Äôs iShares Bitcoin Trust (IBIT), which marked a significant development for spot Bitcoin ETFs. While the Securities and Exchange Commission was initially expected to give its decision on BlackRock Ethereum options trading on Sept. 26, the regulator has now postponed making the ruling to Nov. 10. ‚ÄúThe Commission finds it appropriate to designate a longer period within which to take action on the proposed rule change so that it has sufficient time to consider the proposed rule change,‚Äù the SEC said in a Tuesday press release. In a separate filing, the top Wall Street watchdog also delayed a decision on NYSE American LLC‚Äôs proposed rule change to list and trade options on the Bitwise Ethereum ETF, the Grayscale Ethereum Trust, and the Grayscale Ethereum Mini Trust. The new deadline for NYSE American has been set for Nov. 11. If approved, these options on the ETH ETFs will follow the same listing and trading rules as other trusts, including criteria for underlying securities, expirations, strike prices, and trading halts. The Nasdaq International Securities Exchange submitted a filing with the SEC proposing a rule change to list and trade options tied to BlackRock‚Äôs ETHA on August 6. The move seeks to broaden the range of investment tools for Ethereum and make crypto investments more accessible for traditional investors. The exchange also said the rule change would benefit investors by offering a lower-cost way to gain exposure to the second-largest crypto by market cap, Ether, and meet their investment needs, which generally involve hedging and speculation. For the uninitiated, options are an important vehicle for traders looking to hedge against possible losses in their investments or to bet on the future price of an underlying asset, like a stock or ETF. Options offer flexibility as they give the buyer the right to buy or sell an asset at a set price and on an agreed date. Shortly after Nasdaq‚Äôs filing, NYSE American submitted a proposal to list and trade options on trusts managed by Grayscale and Bitwise. The postponement on Tuesday came after the SEC approved options trading for BlackRock‚Äôs iShares Bitcoin Trust (IBIT) last week. Bloomberg‚Äôs senior ETF analyst Eric Balchunas described the move as a ‚Äúhuge win‚Äù for Bitcoin ETFs as it is expected to attract more liquidity and, subsequently, more ‚Äúbig fish.‚Äù

Title: Bitcoin Analyst Warning: Selling BTC At $73,800 Will Be ‚ÄúDisastrous‚Äù
URL: https://bitcoinist.com/bitcoin-warning-selling-btc-at-73800-disastrous/
Time Published: 2024-09-25T15:30:52Z
Full Content:
Bitcoin is climbing higher when writing, technically bullish but steadying below August highs. Even though there are pockets of strength and the general market sentiment is bullish, looking at the CoinMarketCap poll, buyers should do more. A break above the $65,000 and $66,000 resistance zone could spark a wave of demand that may lift the coin to all-time highs. There will be roadblocks at the $70,000 and $72,000 levels. If buyers take charge and the coin retests to all-time highs, one analyst on X warns that those who sell at that level will be making a ‚Äúdisastrous‚Äù mistake. From his outlook, exiting at around $74,000 will be ‚Äúway too early‚Äù since the coin could rip higher. Technically, the coin remains within a bullish formation. In the monthly chart, buyers are in control despite the dip after the rally to an all-time high in March 2024. Specifically, BTC prices are confined inside a bull flag. A close above the resistance trendline could trigger a lift-off, confirming gains of Q4 2023 and Q1 2024. Though technical candlestick formation may favor bulls, fundamental factors play a crucial role based on the analyst‚Äôs point of view. The analyst argues that selling at around $74,000 will be a mistake because, among other factors, the People‚Äôs Bank of China (PBoC) is propping up the country‚Äôs economy by injecting liquidity. Thus far, the analyst notes that the central bank released their 10-point easing plan to stimulate the struggling Chinese economy. The decision to inject liquidity and slash rates could positively impact the globe. Due to the increasing global liquidity, Bitcoin could benefit from a more accommodative monetary policy from China, Japan, and the United States. Moreover, Bitcoin may find support from the weakening USD index (DXY). As the greenback weakens, other economies, including those in Europe, may choose to support their economies further. The move, in turn, would see capital flow to hard assets like Bitcoin. Already, gold is trending at near all-time highs, and Bitcoin could follow the yellow metal as investors buy them to protect themselves from high inflation. The analyst also pointed out other developments, including the United States approving the application by BlackRock to list and permit the trading of Options for IBIT, their spot Bitcoin ETF. Coupled with banks, including BNY Mellon, showing interest in Bitcoin custody, it could mark the start of fund managers accepting BTC on behalf of their clients. Title: BlackRock‚Äôs head of digital assets says Bitcoin is risky, but still a ‚Äòrisk-off‚Äô asset
URL: https://cryptoslate.com/blackrocks-head-of-digital-assets-says-bitcoin-is-risky-but-still-a-risk-off-asset/
Time Published: 2024-09-25T14:58:15Z
Full Content:
BlackRock exec Robbie Mitchnick believes that the long-term drivers of Bitcoin are significantly different from that of risk-on assets. Cover art/illustration via CryptoSlate. Image includes combined content which may include AI-generated content. BlackRock head of digital assets Robbie Mitchnick believes the crypto industry has made a marketing blunder when it comes to Bitcoin (BTC). Mitchnick said during an interview with Bloomberg that Bitcoin is a risky asset, but calling it a ‚Äúrisk-on‚Äù asset is a mistake akin to an ‚Äúown goal.‚Äù A risk-on asset, like stocks, is something that investors buy when they are optimistic about the market and are willing to take more risk. Therefore, a ‚Äúrisk-off asset‚Äù is where investors move their money when they‚Äôre worried about market volatility. Gold, for example, is considered a risk-off asset because it is likely to hold or increase in value despite economic downturns. Mitchnick said: ‚ÄúSome of the crypto research type publications and daily commentaries have taken the fact that Bitcoin, which is obviously a risky asset, and extrapolated that to say that therefore it is a risk-on asset and should trade like equities.‚Äù He further explained that Bitcoin acts in a fundamentally different way than equities and other risk-on assets. Mitchnick added that the long-term drivers of Bitcoin are ‚Äúvery different‚Äù from other risk-on assets and in some cases, may even be ‚Äúinverted.‚Äù Additionally, Bitcoin does not carry the risks that are usually associated with other risk-on assets. Mitchnick said: ‚ÄúWhen we think about Bitcoin, we think about it primarily as an emerging global monetary alternative‚Äî[a] scarce, global, decentralized, non-sovereign asset. And it‚Äôs an asset that has no country-specific risk, that has no counterparty risk.‚Äù According to Mitchnick, these properties make Bitcoin an intriguing alternative for investors who are concerned about the risks of printing money, currency devaluation, as well as political and fiscal sustainability challenges. Furthermore, its properties are fundamentally different from other risk-on assets, which is why calling Bitcoin a risk-on asset only confuses investors. Mitchnick also pointed out that, like gold, Bitcoin is not correlated to US stocks in the long term. While in the short term, the correlation can spike, on average, it remains ‚Äúpretty close to zero,‚Äù resembling the pattern followed by gold. He further stated that there are only three or four things in a year that actually impact the price of Bitcoin significantly. However, this leaves little scope for publications to create daily stories. Therefore, Mitchnick believes that reporters often instinctively correlate fluctuations in Bitcoin‚Äôs price with the unemployment rate, the stock market, or manufacturing. However, these events and incidents have ‚Äúno connection to Bitcoin.‚Äù Source: CryptoSlate Bitcoin Ecosystem Crypto Sector Data In 2020, Monika immersed herself in crypto, maintaining skepticism yet firmly believing blockchain could address key issues like financial disparity and transparency. Title: Data Centers At The Heart Of The AI And Digital Economy Surge
URL: https://www.forbes.com/sites/emilsayegh/2024/09/25/data-centers-at-the-heart-of-the-ai-and-digital-economy-surge/
Time Published: 2024-09-25T14:52:12Z
Full Content:
Massive Data Center Buildouts Next To Reliable Power And Telecomunication Hubs. Data centers have quietly evolved from obscure server warehouses tucked away in industrial parks to the backbone of our digital society. Once considered dull, gray structures, these facilities have become the critical infrastructure that powers everything we rely on today‚Äîsocial media, artificial intelligence-driven innovations, and daily conveniences like navigation apps and ride-sharing. These high-security buildings are now as essential as highways and airports, connecting us to the digital economy that fuels our lives. However, their newfound importance comes with a host of challenges, and how we respond will dictate the pace of societal progress. The New Digital Frontier It's hard to believe that just a few decades ago, data centers were little more than warehouses for servers, often located in remote or economically disadvantaged areas. The internet boom of the late 1990s put data centers on the map, with companies like Exodus Communications pioneering the concept of large-scale data centers. But as with many tech trends, the early 2000s saw a crash. Overzealous investments led to an overbuild that left many data centers underutilized for years. Fast forward to 2024, and we are witnessing another data center boom. This time, the demand is not only driven by a rapidly expanding internet but by a digital society that never sleeps‚Äîcompounded by artificial intelligence, which is creating an unprecedented need for computing power. Data Centers Matter Now More Than Ever Today, the U.S. data center market is experiencing explosive growth. According to JLL, the market has doubled in size since 2020, with a compound annual growth rate of 21%. Vacancy rates are at an all-time low of 3% and are rapidly approaching zero. According to Houlihan Lokey, this soaring demand is fueling a construction boom, with 5.3 gigawatts (GW) of new capacity under construction as of mid-2024, and 22 GW planned to meet the increasing need for digital infrastructure. But it‚Äôs not just the volume that‚Äôs rising‚Äîcolocation rents, the cost of leasing space within data centers, have surged by as much as 37% year-over-year. No longer just a utility, data centers are now a premium asset in the digital economy. Artificial intelligence is the primary driver behind this data center explosion. AI-related capital expenditures now exceed $300 billion, and the technology accounts for 20% of all new data center demand. Companies like Google, Amazon, and Microsoft are at the forefront, developing hyperscale data centers that stretch the limits of computing power. From self-driving cars to facial recognition, artificial intelligence consumes vast amounts of computational resources. Every time you interact with a digital assistant, use a navigation app, or even send flowers online, you are tapping into the enormous power of a data center. Powering The Future: The Sustainability Crisis This unprecedented demand, however, comes at a cost: electricity. Data centers are massive energy consumers, and as the number of facilities grows, so does the strain on the U.S. power grid. The rise of electric vehicles and increased manufacturing demands further compound the issue, pushing power availability to the brink of crisis. Some estimates suggest that data centers alone could account for 20% of global electricity demand by the end of the decade. To combat this, industry leaders are turning to alternative energy solutions. For example, Amazon Web Services is exploring nuclear energy to power its massive campuses. This race for sustainable solutions isn‚Äôt just about cutting costs‚Äîit‚Äôs about survival in an increasingly energy-hungry world. Investor Confidence Soars Despite these challenges, investor confidence in the data center market remains at an all-time high. Cap rates‚Äîa measure of return on investment in real estate‚Äîhave remained stable between 6-7%, buoyed by strong demand for digital infrastructure and rising rents. Valuations of leading data center companies like Digital Realty Trust and Switch have reached unprecedented levels. Heavyweights such as BlackRock and Microsoft are pouring hundreds of billions into expanding data center infrastructure, signaling that the sector isn‚Äôt just a short-term play‚Äîit‚Äôs a long-term investment in the future of the digital economy. A Call To Action: Building With Purpose, Not Panic The data center industry is poised for a bright future, but it‚Äôs crucial to learn from the mistakes of the past. During the dot-com boom, over-exuberance and a lack of strategic foresight led to a catastrophic overbuild that took years to correct. As we rush to meet today‚Äôs demand, we must plan with purpose. It‚Äôs not enough to simply build more data centers. We need to build them with their specific use case in mind: Is it for hyperscale operations, artificial intelligence processing, or corporate IT? This means situating facilities near reliable power sources and connectivity hubs while ensuring they have access to renewable or responsible energy solutions‚Äîwhether solar, natural gas, or nuclear. The industry cannot afford another bubble, especially with stakes higher than ever before. Thoughtful planning today will set the foundation for sustainable growth tomorrow. Data centers are no longer just the backbone of the internet‚Äîthey are the foundation of our digital world. But with this influence comes responsibility. The decisions we make today about data center construction, energy consumption, and workforce development will shape the digital infrastructure of the future. One Community. Many Voices. Title: Backpedaling On ESG Commitments Will Inevitably Backfire
URL: https://www.forbes.com/sites/adriandearnell/2024/09/25/backpedaling-on-esg-commitments-will-inevitably-backfire/
Time Published: 2024-09-25T14:37:30Z
Full Content:
At a time when many companies are dialing down their prior commitments on sustainability, building trust and maintaining credibility in corporate communication has never been more important. Don't make ESG promises that you don't intend to keep. BlackRock, Unilever, JP Morgan Chase‚Äî the list keeps growing when it comes to ESG backpedaling. And at a time when more eyes than ever are watching for slip-ups, not following through on commitments exposes a company to reputational risks. However, these self-inflicted wounds are avoidable as long as companies recognize the importance of balancing financial performance and ESG commitments, and make a robust internal review before taking a public stand on hot-button topics. BlackRock is learning that lesson now. After announcing a strong stance on ESG in 2020 ,‚Äúcommitted to putting sustainability at the center of our investment process,‚Äù the world‚Äôs largest asset manager recently backed away, citing higher-than-expected costs and lower-than-expected returns on green energy and other ESG-related assets. Larry Fink, BlackRock‚Äôs CEO, explained the change as consistent with the company‚Äôs core mission to maximize returns to investors. ‚ÄúIf a customer wants to invest 100% in decarbonization, and financial profitability is not its priority, we will invest accordingly,‚Äù Fink told the French daily Le Figaro in June 2024. ‚ÄúBut most of our investors want us to provide them with the best financial profitability.‚Äù He added, "In reality, the energy transition is much more complex than we imagined." BlackRock‚Äôs 2024 about-face, versus its 2020 stance, has generated scathing criticism, with the company being accused of having taken an opportunistic stand rather than showing genuine commitment to ESG goals. Of course companies, like individuals, are entitled to change their minds. But those changes should not modify the core of the company‚Äôs values. Values should be unshakeable and not subject to short-term market forces. BlackRock‚Äôs mistake was that it committed to an ESG course of action without fully realizing the implications. Once its ESG commitment was deemed too expensive and threatened to harm financial performance, the company backtracked on what it had previously upheld as a bedrock principle. BlackRock is not alone. JPMorgan Chase CEO Jamie Dimon recently drew sharp criticism from U.S. senators over the bank‚Äôs continued financing of fossil-fuel, despite longstanding public statements in support of battling climate change. Unilever, the British-Dutch consumer goods giant, has been long seen as a leader in sustainability. The new CEO, Hein Schumacher, recently announced the company would be dialing down some of its previously stated ESG targets. Did the backpedaling occur because stock analysts had criticized Unilever for over-emphasizing ESG instead of financial performance? Contrast these companies with the likes of Patagonia, known for its consistent alignment of business practices with environmental values. In its 51-year history, Patagonia has maintained profitability while staying true to its core environmental beliefs. The fact that Patagonia is a small, privately held company no doubt helps it stay insulated from stock-market pressures. However, Costco, the third largest retailer in the world after WalMart and Amazon, regularly features on most-admired lists because of its competitive prices which are founded on good labor practices, good relations with suppliers, and good customer service. Costco‚Äôs net income has risen steadily for the past four years. Writing in Harvard Business Review, Andrew Winston analyzes the types of attacks companies are now facing on ESG and sustainability. While he notes that the criticism may be motivated by different interests, issues, or politics, his advice to companies is largely the same. ‚ÄúDo what fits the values of the company and what seems right.‚Äù Further, ‚ÄúBuild better, more resilient businesses that profit by helping solve big challenges.‚Äù For Coca-Cola CEO James Quincey, merging business practice, values, and corporate communications is simple. ‚Äú‚Ä¶for my basic product, I want to be water positive, I want to have a circular economy on my packaging, and I want to grow our business with less sugar‚Äîyou can call it anything you like, but no one with common sense says those are bad ideas.‚Äù In the corporate world, consistency is still the key to maintaining the trust of investors, employees, suppliers, customers, and other external stakeholders such as ratings agencies and NGOs. So, from a communications standpoint remember to: - Communicate genuine commitment to the company‚Äôs values. - Develop strategies for transparent and consistent communication that build and preserve trust. In a nutshell, say what you do, and do what you say. One Community. Many Voices. Create a free account to share your thoughts. Title: Court Calls The Terms Of Ryan Breslow‚Äôs $450 Million Bolt Deal A ‚ÄòPrisoner‚Äôs Dilemma‚Äô
URL: https://www.forbes.com/sites/sarahemerson/2024/09/25/court-calls-the-terms-of-ryan-breslows-450-million-bolt-deal-a-prisoners-dilemma/
Time Published: 2024-09-25T14:31:52Z
Full Content:
The Delaware Court of Chancery has extended an order stalling Bolt founder Ryan Breslow‚Äôs bid to raise $450 million, characterizing the cram-down round as a ‚Äúprisoner‚Äôs dilemma‚Äù for investors. Bolt's proposed $450 million round would see the young founder return to the company as CEO. Bolt and its cofounder Ryan Breslow were dealt a series of stinging remarks from a Delaware judge last week, during a hearing to continue a temporary restraining order on the company‚Äôs controversial $450 million funding round. The halt on the Series F financing was requested by a trio of irate Bolt investors including the world‚Äôs largest asset manager, BlackRock, and has been extended through mid-October. It is the latest snag in Breslow‚Äôs ongoing bid to raise fresh capital for the struggling payments company. The round, which was first announced in August and would value Bolt at $14 billion, has already been hamstrung by a series of complications that have infuriated shareholders, among them a mixup over the name of its lead investor, and inaccurate claims made by Breslow about who had signed up for the deal. Three weeks ago, a Delaware court approved the restraining order, which Bolt has since tried to lift. ‚ÄúIt's a return of the king for Ryan Breslow,‚Äù said Skadden attorney Cliff Gardner, representing BlackRock, Hedosophia and Untitled Ventures during Wednesday‚Äôs hearing, according to a Delaware Court of Chancery transcript obtained by Forbes. As previously reported by Forbes and others, the unorthodox deal would see Breslow reinstated as Bolt‚Äôs CEO and afford him a large number of benefits, such as a $2 million closing bonus, $80,000 per month for travel and security expenses and a preemptive right to purchase all shares issued in future rounds. ‚ÄúIt should come as no surprise to anyone that I am concerned about an allegation that stockholders of a Delaware corporation are being subject to coercion.‚Äù The terms of the deal, which gave investors just days to buy into the pay-to-play round or see 70% of their shares effectively wiped out, were characterized by Vice Chancellor Nathan Cook as a ‚Äúprisoner‚Äôs dilemma,‚Äù referring to the thought experiment where participants have a chance to either turn on each other or cooperate for a greater, shared prize. Accusing the deal of being coercive and harmful to shareholders, the three investors filed a restraining order to stop the round. The hearing last week was intended to provide Bolt an opportunity to respond. But the court transcript showed the company was unable to provide evidence that resolved the questions and allegations raised by the plaintiffs. ‚ÄúIt should come as no surprise to anyone that I am concerned about an allegation that stockholders of a Delaware corporation are being subject to coercion,‚Äù Cook remarked. ‚ÄúAnd it's been two weeks since our last hearing, and there is no affidavit, no document that anyone can apparently point to that rebuts the allegation.‚Äù An attorney for Bolt called the investors‚Äô claims ‚Äúhyperventilation‚Äù and ‚Äúindignation about the deal that Ryan Breslow is supposed to get out of this.‚Äù They also disputed the allegation that the deal, if approved by shareholders, would push through a broad release of claims against Breslow. When the judge pointed to a document that seemingly showed evidence of the release, the company‚Äôs attorneys said they planned to remove the ‚Äúambiguous‚Äù language. Got a tip for us? Contact reporters Sarah Emerson at semerson@forbes.com or 510-473-8820 on Signal, and Iain Martin at iain.martin@forbes.com. The contours of the confusing deal have continued to evolve. Last month, Forbes reported that a broker accidentally listed investment bank Silverbear Capital as the funding round‚Äôs lead investor, causing a flurry of shareholder confusion. The source of the error was Silverbear partner Brad Pamnani, who claimed to have used the wrong email address to sign a Bolt nondisclosure agreement. The broker, AMA Investment Group, told Forbes that it would be issuing corrected financial documents with the name of the actual lead investor, but according to last week‚Äôs hearing, no new paperwork has been provided ‚Äî a fact the plaintiffs argued could prove troubling if they seek legal action against Pamnani, who is claiming to represent an unnamed Abu Dhabi-based fund, which could fall outside the Delaware court‚Äôs jurisdiction. ‚ÄúIf I'm looking at this with the lightest touch‚Ä¶it would seem to me that whatever it is that's going on with Silverbear Capital is problematic from a disclosure standpoint,‚Äù said Judge Cook. Now, the plaintiffs are hoping to obtain testimony from Breslow, Bolt and some of its new backers. ‚ÄúWe intend to depose Mr. Pamnani at a later stage and find out why he is confused about Silverbear's participation,‚Äù said Gardner, the plaintiffs‚Äô attorney. Pamnani previously told Forbes that the error about Silverbear‚Äôs role was merely administrative. Bolt has since threatened the bank with legal action to hold it to the ‚Äúbinding term sheet‚Äù Pamnani signed. Silverbear partner Veronica Welch told Forbes she was unaware of the temporary restraining order, and said their team is currently working with Bolt ‚Äúto come up with a solution that will enable us to all move forward together in a positive way.‚Äù Still, Bolt pushed for the injunction to be lifted, warning that the payments company was losing market share, and the lawsuit could stall the planned October launch of Bolt‚Äôs ‚Äúsuper app.‚Äù But it struggled to explain the terms of the deal to the court, which include $250 million of ‚Äúmarketing credits‚Äù from an obscure venture fund with an influencer marketing startup. ‚ÄúI am beseeching you to identify somewhere in these documents that this deal actually works the way you are saying it works,‚Äù said Cook. In slides submitted to the court, the plaintiffs also detailed previously unreported elements of Bolt‚Äôs Series F round. For example, should the deal go through, Pamnani is set to receive compensation representing 250,000 shares of Class A Common Stock, while Bolt board member and gaming startup founder Michael Carter, who has known Breslow since his days at Stanford University, will receive options representing 1.8 million shares of Class A Common Stock. The shareholders continued to protest a settlement between Breslow and Bolt investor Activant Capital. Last year, Activant sued the founder over a $30 million loan he had secured with Bolt‚Äôs money and subsequently defaulted on. Both parties eventually agreed to a settlement that would cancel a commensurate number of Breslow‚Äôs shares as repayment, and would see Bolt repurchase Activant‚Äôs entire stake in the company. It also included a ‚Äútrue-up provision‚Äù that would hand Breslow a block of Bolt A or B shares worth $37.3 million if the startup raised at least $75 million in a new round by the end of the year. BlackRock and its co-plaintiffs objected to the agreement in July, accusing Breslow of using company funds to pay off his dissenters, and now argue the settlement should be halted under the restraining order. Last week, Breslow and Activant filed a joint appeal to allow the share cancellation and buyout to go through. ‚ÄúI want to pause and say those of us who are on the outside of the board, the plaintiffs, now it's just so utterly obvious this has been choreographed for all this time,‚Äù said Gardener. ‚ÄúWhen that settlement agreement came in ‚Äî and I recall, I read that true-up provision, and I thought, boy, they must have this one cooking in the background.‚Äù Bolt and the investors are now fighting over the date of an upcoming preliminary injunction hearing next month. There will also be an expedited discovery process, wherein Bolt will be expected to produce internal documentation detailing the funding round. The investors pushed for a full trial next year but the company has asked the court to accept an earlier date ‚Äúto accommodate sensitive business timing‚Äù issues. Bolt declined to comment, and Activant did not respond to a comment request.

Title: Skipping Coren Direbrew for the Halls of Origination
URL: https://tagn.wordpress.com/2024/09/25/skipping-coren-direbrew-for-the-halls-of-origination/
Time Published: 2024-09-25T14:15:40Z
Full Content:
Brewfest is back up in classic, with the Cataclysm level 85 rewards now part of the mix, so when the group got online on Sunday the thought was that we might pay a visit to our old friend Coren Direbrew for a bit of gearing up. Gearing up, as I mentioned in the previous post this week, was on our agenda. Camping the Horde trying to earn honor So we got all grouped up and I went to the dungeon finder and selected Coren Direbrew, who is in there as his own entry and‚Ä¶ got told that Ula needed a level. Ula is not high enough level Looking at the group comp, she was not yet level 85 and still had a good six chiclets, 30% of a level, to go. We were not going to get that done quickly. The group this week Everything I saw online said you should be able to queue for Coren at level 84, but the DF was saying 85 was the minimum, and it makes the rules. So we went to Plan B and decided to just GO TO Blackrock Depths, where the Grim Guzzler is located, to visit Coren Direbrew in person. A couple of flew out to Blackrock Mountain, got to the summoning stone, then summoned the remainder, and then the group began the trot down to Blackrock Depths, a location we visited no fewer than a dozen times during vanilla. Once we got in, we had to figure out how to get to the Grim Guzzler. There was a Dark Iron transport, a ‚Äúscrew house‚Äù in the vernacular of our group, which offered a couple of options which corresponded to the new, broken into nice bite sized adventures, that is the reality of BRD in the era of Cataclsym, neither of which got us where we needed to go. One was just past the Grim Guzzler, but the door was locked and nobody had the key, and the other was down a different path that wouldn‚Äôt help us. So we just went old school and ran to the bar. And when we got there, no Coren Direbrew was there to be seen. I mean, the Tauren Chieften‚Äôs band kit was still there, the kegs were still there, we were in the right location within BRD, just not where Coren was. Potshot remembered that last time around we got a little device that would summon a screw house and send us to Coren. I had one back in the bank, so UIa put up a portal to Ironforge so I could go get it, then there was a ritual of summoning by Liftkit to return me to the instance. I activated the control, a screw house appeared, and it deposited us about ten feet across the room. Such a distance! It seems that Coren now exists in his own instance than can only be reached via the Dungeon Finder and we were not going to get to him. His upgrades would have to wait. So we said screw it and I queued us up for the Halls or Origination, which was the next instance on our Cataclysm list. Off we went. Kids in the Hall! Seven bosses! It was going to be an event! But at least the in-game dungeon guide gives you a scorecard so you can be sure to collect them all. Today‚Äôs boss lineup Into the instance the map only showed two bosses, so we were clearly going to be moving around. The opening map of the instance Fortunately, the path was pretty clear to the first boss. We struggled a little bit with the trash mob groups after two weeks away, but that was sufficient warm up to get us to Temple Guardian Anhuur. Anhuur, the first boss on the list The in-game guide was good enough to give us some useful tips on the fight mechanics‚Ä¶ specifically, that twice during the fight Anhuur will put up a barrier that will make him invulnerable and to get past that somebody has to run downstairs and trip two switches before the fight can resume. The switches, to left and right, marked by Potshot There are some snakes down there‚Ä¶ non-elite‚Ä¶ that we tried to clear, but somebody thought about that dodge and they respawn quickly. Still, it seemed doable. Ula took one switch, Liftkit the other, and off we went. And it seemed to work. When Anhuur is invulnerable he also doesn‚Äôt deal out much damage, so we had time. The fight went by quickly enough and soon it was one boss down. Anhuur down in 2 minutes and 52 seconds Among other things, the Deadly Boss Mods addon gives you a fight timer. I don‚Äôt know that we set any records, but I‚Äôll record the times for posterity. As for drops, he had a nice mail item, and nobody in our group wears mail, so one for Ula to disenchant. Past Anhuur we hit that big round room on the map, which is an elevator. However, it wasn‚Äôt letting us go anywhere, so we went to the left towards the Vault of Lights on the map where we ran into Bann Bronzebeard at the door to the area. Oh, hey Brann‚Ä¶ you going to open that for us? He did oblige and open it and gave us a song and dance about getting to the door at the far side, which meant eliminating a mini boss in each of the four along the way, while fending off roving groups or quickly respawning troggs. The troggs turned out to be, if not soap bubbles, then at least not really as elite as their designations otherwise indicated. And the mini bosses were not so bad either. On eliminating the last one the door at the far end opened and Anraphet stepped out, banished the troggs, and then waited for us to make out move. Anraphet awaits Having done well reading up on the first boss we got a little deep into trying to decipher how to do every fight going forward‚Ä¶ though, in the end, save for an odd mechanic here and there, the solution tended to be ‚Äúmore DPS‚Äù to just finish things. And so went Anraphet, who at least dropped something useful. Modest breastplate upgrade for Fergorin We then followed Brann into the room where‚Ä¶ he didn‚Äôt do much. So Brann‚Ä¶ you brought us all here‚Ä¶ With no buttons to press or further dialog to deal with, we went back the way we came, back to the elevator. However, I looked at the boss list and it seemed like we skipped somebody. So we went down the hallway that kind of fades on the map and found Earthrager Ptah. Ptah was waiting for us There are some camels you can ride to get to him, however when you dismount them they die, which was a bit disturbing. Ptah‚Äôs guide said that mid-fight he would summon some adds that we would need to defeat before the fight could resume‚Ä¶ so we did. We managed to wrap him up in just under two minutes. Ptah done in 1 minute and 59 seconds Ptah did a nice staff that our two casters did a need-off to get. Ptah‚Äôs parting gift Ula won the roll and walked away with a shiny new staff. That done it was back to the elevator which now offered us an option to go to the second floor, which offered us a selection of bosses. Second floor, four ways Now, if I had been paying close attention to the boss list in the guide we would have gone magic, life, destruction, then radiance. But we happened to be facing north so we went to the first boss we saw, Rajh the Construct of the Sun, which I guess applies to ‚Äúradiance‚Äù but also it would be nice if they would use the same terminology across the board. Anyway, him. Welcome to the sun‚Ä¶ or Radiance‚Ä¶ or Rajh He had several ominous sounding attacks and a whole portion of the fight where he would deliver unavoidable AOE but also take double damage and we were working out how to heal through it and making sure everybody had potions and such. And then the fight happened, he got to that part and I started just shouting ‚ÄúMore DPS!‚Äù (DOTs being irrelevant) and then he was dead. Rajh laid out before us That also triggered the achievement for the instance because we did the last boss first. Are we there yet? That done, we went after the other three. Eschewing any order, we went for destruction next, facing Setesh. Setesh has a nice style The trash before him caused us to wipe. It turns out that they lay down gunk that heals them and damages you, so you need to kite them around. Instead I just sat there as we burned through all of Fergorin‚Äôs mana, all my cool downs, and whatever else we had before we were all dead. Ula, last alive, started to kite them and made some progress, which was the lightbulb moment. Once revived and restored‚Ä¶ that guild perk ress is very handy‚Ä¶ Liftkit banished one of the trash mobs and I kited the other around and they were dead in about a minute. It helps to do the right thing. Setesh himself had a whole routine where you can‚Äôt tank him, he just summons adds and you‚Äôre supposed to take them down, and crystals the DPS are supposed to stand in to boost their damage, and probably something else I am forgetting. It was all a distraction. We got deep into the fight and the adds were getting out of control and I called to just kill him while I tried to collect all the adds‚Ä¶ and that did it. Setech also dropped a nice healer mace for Fergorin. Scepter for Fergorin Two down. Magic was up next, with Isiset. We had a bit of trouble with her trash too, but I managed to step out of the beam of death that was killing me before I caused another wipe. Isiset and the house of magic Isiset has a mechanic where twice during the fight she splits up into her three abilities the first time, and the ability you kill is removed from the fight while the other two get a buff. When that hit I chose the ability where she summons adds, which seemed like the best call. So no adds to worry about. I don‚Äôt even remember which ability I chose on the second round I was so happy to not deal with adds. And, we finished her off. That left us with Ammunae, the construct of life. Ammunae awaits us Another fight with another gimmick, this time pods you needed to kill lest they become elite adds. More adds. Why does it always have to be adds? Anyway, we did Ammunae like the Tide pod challenge and that was that. We had finished it off The group post instance I later went back and looked at the blog post from our run at the instance back in 2014 and‚Ä¶ we did almost exactly the same thing. We even wiped on the same trash mobs and did the last boss first. I guess we are predictable. Done with the instance we asked Ula for a portal to Stormwind, so she wound up and‚Ä¶ disappeared. Ula now missing from the scene Out of practice for a couple of weeks, she mixed up the left click, right click thing for portals versus teleports. Liftkit then used the Dungeon Finder to leave the instance‚Ä¶ and ended up back in Blackrock Depths which is where we were when we queued for the dungeon. Fergorin, Kharageenan, and I decided to just hearthstone back to Dalaran‚Ä¶ because of course our stones are still set there. Time to hearth on out That leaves us with just the Lost City of Tol‚Äôvir on the list of normal mode dungeons to complete. Of course, there is still Coren Direbrew. Ula should be 85 by the next time we get together. Halls of Origination is the reason why I stopped queuing for random dungeons ‚Äìnormal or heroic‚Äì in Retail. I got into my first HoO run, zoned in, and told people there that this was my first time there, and‚Ä¶ I was ignored. People just ran ahead and did the instance, assuming that everybody knew what was supposed to be done, and I basically ran around like a chicken with my head cut off trying to just do damage where I could. To this day I still don‚Äôt know how that instance is supposed to work. I guess I should feel grateful that I wasn‚Äôt kicked and that the instance is marked ‚Äúcompleted‚Äù somewhere, but I certainly don‚Äôt feel like I actually participated in the dungeon. That was when I decided to stop queuing for random instances and either stick to the ones I knew or just stop running PvE group content entirely. So kudos to you and your group for completing that instance and figuring it out. LikeLike I am just amused that we made all the same mistakes as we did a decade back. Some might suggest that I should read the old posts BEFORE we do an instance again, but where is the fun in that? LikeLike Œî Email Address: Email Posts to Me! Title: Call It Greenflation ‚Äî And Kamala Wants More Of It
URL: https://freerepublic.com/focus/f-chat/4267013/posts
Time Published: 2024-09-25T13:44:37Z
Full Content:
Skip to comments. Posted on 09/25/2024 6:44:37 AM PDT by MtnClimber For families struggling to make ends meet, Kamala Harris claims she has a plan to lower energy costs. What she will deliver is more pain. Just ask anyone paying energy bills in a state her party controls. On Harris‚Äô campaign website, she pays lip service to reducing energy costs, but then rattles off a long list of plans to tackle the ‚Äúclimate crisis.‚Äù We already know you can‚Äôt have one with the other. At a congressional hearing last week, members of the House Budget Committee heard from witnesses about how Biden-Harris policies have fueled today‚Äôs energy crisis. One of the witnesses, Diana Furchtgott-Roth of the Heritage Foundation, presented lawmakers with a chart that deserves to be seen by anyone and everyone paying utility bills. The chart ranks states based on the cost of electricity, as well as the cost of a gallon of gas. Looking at the chart, you immediately notice something. Of the 16 states where electricity costs are higher than the national average, Republicans control only two. All the rest are either completely or partially run by Democrats. Why are their energy bills so high? Well, all but two have imposed strict mandates for renewable energy ‚Äì meaning that more than 15% of their electricity will have to come from ‚Äúclean‚Äù sources by 2035. What‚Äôs more, all but six also want 100% of cars sold in the state to be EVs by 2035. In other words, these Blue states are fully bought into the climate ‚Äúcrisis.‚Äù (Republican-controlled Alaska is an outlier because it has its own unique energy challenges.) Meanwhile, of the 10 states with the lowest electricity rates, only Washington is controlled by Democrats. It has a strict renewable standard, and an EV mandate. But as Furtchgott-Roth notes, Washington is also a special case because 60% of its energy comes from hydropower (a cheap and ‚Äúclean‚Äù energy source that environmentalists hate because it requires damming rivers). The difference in household utility bills between these Blue and Red states is stark, with Californians paying nearly three times what Louisianans do, for example. And this is just the beginning. Wait until those costly renewable mandates ‚Äì combined with the surge in electricity demand that will result from state EV mandates and the growth of artificial intelligence ‚Äì are in full force. Then Blue-state electricity costs will be stratospheric. Keep in mind, too, that higher energy prices impact everything you buy because energy costs affect every business, and those costs are always passed down to consumers. So the overall cost of living in Blue states is higher as a result. At the same time, the chart above also shows that gasoline prices tend to be higher in these Blue states. Sometimes much, much higher. A gallon of gasoline in California costs $4.75, but only $3.18 in Florida. These price differences, too, are largely caused by taxes and regulations. What are those ratepayers and drivers in Blue states getting for all those extra costs? Nothing. Politicians in these states pass laws pushed by radical environmentalists to make themselves feel good. The costs are paid for by working families already struggling to make ends meet. And the impact on the climate is ‚Ä¶ zero. Even if every state in the nation went 100% renewable, it wouldn‚Äôt make a bit of difference to global temperatures, given that China and India are pumping out more CO2 each year than the U.S. could possibly ever cut. The question Democrats need to answer is ‚ÄúWhy do they hate their residents so much?‚Äù But residents also need to ask themselves why they put up with such lunacy. Our guess is that most of them don‚Äôt know they‚Äôre being royally screwed. The problem is that, no matter what Harris claims today, she desperately wants to make the entire country like those Blue states. Which is another reason why every American should see (and share) the chart before they vote in November. Well, all but two have imposed strict mandates for renewable energy ‚Äì meaning that more than 15% of their electricity will have to come from ‚Äúclean‚Äù sources by 2035. What‚Äôs more, all but six also want 100% of cars sold in the state to be EVs by 2035. In other words, these Blue states are fully bought into the climate ‚Äúcrisis.‚Äù (Republican-controlled Alaska is an outlier because it has its own unique energy challenges.) Meanwhile, of the 10 states with the lowest electricity rates, only Washington is controlled by Democrats. It has a strict renewable standard, and an EV mandate. But as Furtchgott-Roth notes, Washington is also a special case because 60% of its energy comes from hydropower (a cheap and ‚Äúclean‚Äù energy source that environmentalists hate because it requires damming rivers). The difference in household utility bills between these Blue and Red states is stark, with Californians paying nearly three times what Louisianans do, for example. And this is just the beginning. Wait until those costly renewable mandates ‚Äì combined with the surge in electricity demand that will result from state EV mandates and the growth of artificial intelligence ‚Äì are in full force. Then Blue-state electricity costs will be stratospheric. Keep in mind, too, that higher energy prices impact everything you buy because energy costs affect every business, and those costs are always passed down to consumers. So the overall cost of living in Blue states is higher as a result. At the same time, the chart above also shows that gasoline prices tend to be higher in these Blue states. Sometimes much, much higher. A gallon of gasoline in California costs $4.75, but only $3.18 in Florida. These price differences, too, are largely caused by taxes and regulations. What are those ratepayers and drivers in Blue states getting for all those extra costs? Nothing. Politicians in these states pass laws pushed by radical environmentalists to make themselves feel good. The costs are paid for by working families already struggling to make ends meet. And the impact on the climate is ‚Ä¶ zero. Even if every state in the nation went 100% renewable, it wouldn‚Äôt make a bit of difference to global temperatures, given that China and India are pumping out more CO2 each year than the U.S. could possibly ever cut. The question Democrats need to answer is ‚ÄúWhy do they hate their residents so much?‚Äù But residents also need to ask themselves why they put up with such lunacy. Our guess is that most of them don‚Äôt know they‚Äôre being royally screwed. The problem is that, no matter what Harris claims today, she desperately wants to make the entire country like those Blue states. Which is another reason why every American should see (and share) the chart before they vote in November. Free Republic Browse ¬∑ Search General/Chat Topics ¬∑ Post Article FreeRepublic, LLC, PO BOX 9771, FRESNO, CA 93794 FreeRepublic.com is powered by software copyright 2000-2008 John Robinson We already know you can‚Äôt have one with the other. At a congressional hearing last week, members of the House Budget Committee heard from witnesses about how Biden-Harris policies have fueled today‚Äôs energy crisis. One of the witnesses, Diana Furchtgott-Roth of the Heritage Foundation, presented lawmakers with a chart that deserves to be seen by anyone and everyone paying utility bills. The chart ranks states based on the cost of electricity, as well as the cost of a gallon of gas. Looking at the chart, you immediately notice something. Of the 16 states where electricity costs are higher than the national average, Republicans control only two. All the rest are either completely or partially run by Democrats. Why are their energy bills so high? Well, all but two have imposed strict mandates for renewable energy ‚Äì meaning that more than 15% of their electricity will have to come from ‚Äúclean‚Äù sources by 2035. What‚Äôs more, all but six also want 100% of cars sold in the state to be EVs by 2035. In other words, these Blue states are fully bought into the climate ‚Äúcrisis.‚Äù (Republican-controlled Alaska is an outlier because it has its own unique energy challenges.) Meanwhile, of the 10 states with the lowest electricity rates, only Washington is controlled by Democrats. It has a strict renewable standard, and an EV mandate. But as Furtchgott-Roth notes, Washington is also a special case because 60% of its energy comes from hydropower (a cheap and ‚Äúclean‚Äù energy source that environmentalists hate because it requires damming rivers). The difference in household utility bills between these Blue and Red states is stark, with Californians paying nearly three times what Louisianans do, for example. And this is just the beginning. Wait until those costly renewable mandates ‚Äì combined with the surge in electricity demand that will result from state EV mandates and the growth of artificial intelligence ‚Äì are in full force. Then Blue-state electricity costs will be stratospheric. Keep in mind, too, that higher energy prices impact everything you buy because energy costs affect every business, and those costs are always passed down to consumers. So the overall cost of living in Blue states is higher as a result. At the same time, the chart above also shows that gasoline prices tend to be higher in these Blue states. Sometimes much, much higher. A gallon of gasoline in California costs $4.75, but only $3.18 in Florida. These price differences, too, are largely caused by taxes and regulations. What are those ratepayers and drivers in Blue states getting for all those extra costs? Nothing. Politicians in these states pass laws pushed by radical environmentalists to make themselves feel good. The costs are paid for by working families already struggling to make ends meet. And the impact on the climate is ‚Ä¶ zero. Even if every state in the nation went 100% renewable, it wouldn‚Äôt make a bit of difference to global temperatures, given that China and India are pumping out more CO2 each year than the U.S. could possibly ever cut. The question Democrats need to answer is ‚ÄúWhy do they hate their residents so much?‚Äù But residents also need to ask themselves why they put up with such lunacy. Our guess is that most of them don‚Äôt know they‚Äôre being royally screwed. The problem is that, no matter what Harris claims today, she desperately wants to make the entire country like those Blue states. Which is another reason why every American should see (and share) the chart before they vote in November. What are those ratepayers and drivers in Blue states getting for all those extra costs? Nothing. Politicians in these states pass laws pushed by radical environmentalists to make themselves feel good. The costs are paid for by working families already struggling to make ends meet. And the impact on the climate is ‚Ä¶ zero. Even if every state in the nation went 100% renewable, it wouldn‚Äôt make a bit of difference to global temperatures, given that China and India are pumping out more CO2 each year than the U.S. could possibly ever cut. The question Democrats need to answer is ‚ÄúWhy do they hate their residents so much?‚Äù But residents also need to ask themselves why they put up with such lunacy. Our guess is that most of them don‚Äôt know they‚Äôre being royally screwed. The problem is that, no matter what Harris claims today, she desperately wants to make the entire country like those Blue states. Which is another reason why every American should see (and share) the chart before they vote in November. Free Republic Browse ¬∑ Search General/Chat Topics ¬∑ Post Article FreeRepublic, LLC, PO BOX 9771, FRESNO, CA 93794 FreeRepublic.com is powered by software copyright 2000-2008 John Robinson Looking at the chart, you immediately notice something. Of the 16 states where electricity costs are higher than the national average, Republicans control only two. All the rest are either completely or partially run by Democrats. Why are their energy bills so high? Well, all but two have imposed strict mandates for renewable energy ‚Äì meaning that more than 15% of their electricity will have to come from ‚Äúclean‚Äù sources by 2035. What‚Äôs more, all but six also want 100% of cars sold in the state to be EVs by 2035. In other words, these Blue states are fully bought into the climate ‚Äúcrisis.‚Äù (Republican-controlled Alaska is an outlier because it has its own unique energy challenges.) Meanwhile, of the 10 states with the lowest electricity rates, only Washington is controlled by Democrats. It has a strict renewable standard, and an EV mandate. But as Furtchgott-Roth notes, Washington is also a special case because 60% of its energy comes from hydropower (a cheap and ‚Äúclean‚Äù energy source that environmentalists hate because it requires damming rivers). The difference in household utility bills between these Blue and Red states is stark, with Californians paying nearly three times what Louisianans do, for example. And this is just the beginning. Wait until those costly renewable mandates ‚Äì combined with the surge in electricity demand that will result from state EV mandates and the growth of artificial intelligence ‚Äì are in full force. Then Blue-state electricity costs will be stratospheric. Keep in mind, too, that higher energy prices impact everything you buy because energy costs affect every business, and those costs are always passed down to consumers. So the overall cost of living in Blue states is higher as a result. At the same time, the chart above also shows that gasoline prices tend to be higher in these Blue states. Sometimes much, much higher. A gallon of gasoline in California costs $4.75, but only $3.18 in Florida. These price differences, too, are largely caused by taxes and regulations. What are those ratepayers and drivers in Blue states getting for all those extra costs? Nothing. Politicians in these states pass laws pushed by radical environmentalists to make themselves feel good. The costs are paid for by working families already struggling to make ends meet. And the impact on the climate is ‚Ä¶ zero. Even if every state in the nation went 100% renewable, it wouldn‚Äôt make a bit of difference to global temperatures, given that China and India are pumping out more CO2 each year than the U.S. could possibly ever cut. The question Democrats need to answer is ‚ÄúWhy do they hate their residents so much?‚Äù But residents also need to ask themselves why they put up with such lunacy. Our guess is that most of them don‚Äôt know they‚Äôre being royally screwed. The problem is that, no matter what Harris claims today, she desperately wants to make the entire country like those Blue states. Which is another reason why every American should see (and share) the chart before they vote in November. Meanwhile, of the 10 states with the lowest electricity rates, only Washington is controlled by Democrats. It has a strict renewable standard, and an EV mandate. But as Furtchgott-Roth notes, Washington is also a special case because 60% of its energy comes from hydropower (a cheap and ‚Äúclean‚Äù energy source that environmentalists hate because it requires damming rivers). The difference in household utility bills between these Blue and Red states is stark, with Californians paying nearly three times what Louisianans do, for example. And this is just the beginning. Wait until those costly renewable mandates ‚Äì combined with the surge in electricity demand that will result from state EV mandates and the growth of artificial intelligence ‚Äì are in full force. Then Blue-state electricity costs will be stratospheric. Keep in mind, too, that higher energy prices impact everything you buy because energy costs affect every business, and those costs are always passed down to consumers. So the overall cost of living in Blue states is higher as a result. At the same time, the chart above also shows that gasoline prices tend to be higher in these Blue states. Sometimes much, much higher. A gallon of gasoline in California costs $4.75, but only $3.18 in Florida. These price differences, too, are largely caused by taxes and regulations. What are those ratepayers and drivers in Blue states getting for all those extra costs? Nothing. Politicians in these states pass laws pushed by radical environmentalists to make themselves feel good. The costs are paid for by working families already struggling to make ends meet. And the impact on the climate is ‚Ä¶ zero. Even if every state in the nation went 100% renewable, it wouldn‚Äôt make a bit of difference to global temperatures, given that China and India are pumping out more CO2 each year than the U.S. could possibly ever cut. The question Democrats need to answer is ‚ÄúWhy do they hate their residents so much?‚Äù But residents also need to ask themselves why they put up with such lunacy. Our guess is that most of them don‚Äôt know they‚Äôre being royally screwed. The problem is that, no matter what Harris claims today, she desperately wants to make the entire country like those Blue states. Which is another reason why every American should see (and share) the chart before they vote in November. And this is just the beginning. Wait until those costly renewable mandates ‚Äì combined with the surge in electricity demand that will result from state EV mandates and the growth of artificial intelligence ‚Äì are in full force. Then Blue-state electricity costs will be stratospheric. Keep in mind, too, that higher energy prices impact everything you buy because energy costs affect every business, and those costs are always passed down to consumers. So the overall cost of living in Blue states is higher as a result. At the same time, the chart above also shows that gasoline prices tend to be higher in these Blue states. Sometimes much, much higher. A gallon of gasoline in California costs $4.75, but only $3.18 in Florida. These price differences, too, are largely caused by taxes and regulations. What are those ratepayers and drivers in Blue states getting for all those extra costs? Nothing. Politicians in these states pass laws pushed by radical environmentalists to make themselves feel good. The costs are paid for by working families already struggling to make ends meet. And the impact on the climate is ‚Ä¶ zero. Even if every state in the nation went 100% renewable, it wouldn‚Äôt make a bit of difference to global temperatures, given that China and India are pumping out more CO2 each year than the U.S. could possibly ever cut. The question Democrats need to answer is ‚ÄúWhy do they hate their residents so much?‚Äù But residents also need to ask themselves why they put up with such lunacy. Our guess is that most of them don‚Äôt know they‚Äôre being royally screwed. Which is another reason why every American should see (and share) the chart before they vote in November. Title: Tucker Carlson Praises Alex Jones as ‚ÄòVindicated on Everything‚Äô ‚Äî Blasts Critics Who Call Him ‚ÄòDangerous‚Äô ‚Äî¬†in Wild Joint Appearance
URL: https://www.mediaite.com/news/tucker-carlson-praises-alex-jones-as-vindicated-on-everything-blasts-critics-who-call-him-dangerous-in-wild-joint-appearance/
Time Published: 2024-09-25T13:31:50Z
Full Content:
Former Fox News host and MAGA commentator Tucker Carlson praised conspiracy theorist Alex Jones as ‚Äúvindicated on everything‚Äù in a wild national tour stop in Pennsylvania on Tuesday. Carlson talked first with right-wing political activist Jack Posobiec but it was Jones who received the rockstar welcome on-stage to roaring applause from the audience.
